Today, I filed HR947, a bipartisan bill to make SSI extensive to the Americans in Puerto Rico and the other territories who are currently suffering this unequal and indignant treatment. This bill is a temporary fix; the only true, permanent solution is Statehood.
Discrimination in SSI affects the most poor and vulnerable of our citizens the elderly, the blind, &amp; the disabled
I welcome Judge Gelpí’s decision, which sheds light on how our territorial status allows our residents to be turned into second class citizens merely because of where they live.

Watch now: I’m speaking on my ammendments to the Disaster Supplemental @RulesReps https://t.co/llqHS5neZi
Puerto Rico has 280,000 Medicare Advantage (MA) enrollees, equal to the 97% of all DUALS. My amendment proposes changes to mitigate the increasing disparity when using the unique and deficient fee-for-service Medicare program in Puerto Rico as the basis for MA rates.
My fourth amendment creates a set-aside for the territories and non-contiguous states affected by natural disasters in 2017 &amp; 2018. This will address the high cost of construction due and will provide more infrastructure funding to address increased costs.
Puerto Rico has had billions of dollars appropriated for disaster relief but those funds have been slow to get where they need to be. My amendment is intended to create transparency of Federal Disaster Funds.
Census reports 95% of the island as low-income but this data reported is from years before Hurricanes Irma and Maria hit Puerto Rico. My amendment provides that Puerto Rico shall be certified and designated as an Opportunity Zone in its entirety.
As Puerto Rico is projected to hit a #Medicaid Cliff, I asked Rules Committee to increase Medicaid funds available to the Island for fiscal years 2020 and 2021.

60% of the beaches in the 799 miles of the coasts of Puerto Rico exhibit some type of erosion. These studies allow us to establish projects to protect the properties, assets, economy and life of visitors and the 2.3 million residents of the 44 coastal municipalities. https://t.co/dFxTJmoWjw
The owners of the hotel Villa Cofresí in Rincón told us how the sea has gained ground over the years, retreating the coastline. Rincón is one of the municipalities where coastal erosion is very evident. https://t.co/hHLobqecLu
These studies on coastal erosion in Puerto Rico are the first carried out on the island by the federal government in its history. We achieved an allocation of funds that had been waiting since 1970 and this week the public hearings began in Aguadilla and San Juan. https://t.co/kYHsrMUCOI
We managed to allocate funds for studies on coastal erosion in the federal Law 115-123, funds that had been expected since 1970 covering 100% of the costs for studies in the metro area, the entire island and the erosion protection project in Loíza that totals $10.5 million. https://t.co/tndRlaPhDd

Los pagos de WHIP se desembolsarán en 2 fases: un pago inicial del 50% del pago elegible; el pago restante se hará después de la fecha de radicación de solicitudes, una vez se haya establecido un factor de pago y después de finalizar todas las acciones administrativas https://t.co/zBADIvb8Dn
Los agricultores pueden solicitar la ayuda provista bajo el programa WHIP que de aprobarse su solicitud pudieran recibir hasta $125,000 por individuo o entidad legal o bajo una aprobación especial de hasta $900,000. https://t.co/fwEDrOFzDu
El programa WHIP cubre tanto la pérdida del cultivo, árbol, arbusto o enredadera. La Agencia federal de Servicio Agrícola, ente administrador del programa, comunicó que se aplicarán disposiciones especiales en la administración de WHIP en Puerto Rico. https://t.co/JyrUGssDl4

For more information on hurricane season preparedness visit https://t.co/DXKmCgUBWO.
• Download the FEMA app to receive weather alerts.		Now is the time to be prepared!  If you or someone in your family is experiencing issues with disaster-related stress, call Línea PAS at 800-981-0023, TTY 888-672-7622.
STAY INFORMED: Listen for up-to-date information 	• Local media will provide evacuation and shelters details.	• Make sure your battery-powered radio is working and you have extra batteries.
• Save a few dollars each week and spread out your shopping for your 10 days’ worth of supplies.	• Switch your Social Security or other regular benefits to electronic payments that are deposited directly into your account.
• Whether you’re a homeowner or renter, contact your insurance agent to ensure you’re adequately covered for housing, car and flooding.	• Keep some cash in hand, in large and small bills.
• In mass care shelters, pets will be taken to a reserved space. Certified service pets are allowed to stay with their owners for emotional support.		BE FINANCIALLY PREPARED: Consider the costs associated with disasters	• Anticipate out-of-pocket expenses for lodging, food, gas
PROTECT YOUR PETS: Make sure someone is available to care of your pets if you can’t	• Get food, water and a collar with identification tag.	• Keep pets inside the house or take them to a pre-identified safe location.
• If relying on public transportation, contact your local emergency agencies about evacuation procedures.	• If you plan to stay at home, make sure it is in good repair and have the plywood, steel or aluminum panels to board up windows and doors.
• Keep important phone numbers with you at all times.		ASSESS YOUR SHELTERING NEEDS: Identify where you will shelter 	• Identify where you will shelter in case you are ordered to leave your home, and share the location with your family.
MAKE A FAMILY PLAN: Identify alternate ways to stay in touch with loved ones 	• Choose an out of town friend or relative as a point of contact.	• Decide on a meeting place in case you cannot return home.
BUILD A KIT: Be sure you have at least 10 days of supplies	• Store a gallon of water, food, prescriptions and other supplies per person per day. Pay special attention to infants, the elderly and people with disabilities and access and functional needs.
Are You Ready for Hurricane Season? 		Here are some tips to get ready for hurricane season from FEMA:

Watch me speak against the cockfight ban in the territories. This sport is sufficiently regulated in Puerto Rico. The Farm Bill failed to pass, so the ban was unsuccessful. Cockfighting will continue. https://t.co/r9KzUKyHFi
Prohibir abruptamente las peleas de gallos transformaría una industria altamente regulada en una industria subterránea, trayendo las peleas a nuestras calles donde no podríamos garantizar el control y los altos estándares de regulación que se tienen actualmente. https://t.co/TP1dHoFcA1
Según las últimas estadísticas de la Oficina de Asuntos Gallísticos de Puerto Rico, esta industria representa:	• Aproximadamente 27 mil empleos directos e indirectos.	• Y más de $18 millones en actividad económica.
En Puerto Rico, las peleas de gallos ya son una industria de juegos altamente regulada. La Ley 98-2007, creó la Oficina de Asuntos Gallísticos bajo el Departamento de Recreación y Deportes de Puerto Rico.
Hoy, me opuse tenazmente en el Hemiciclo Federal a la enmienda número 28 que busca prohibir las peleas de gallos en los territorios. https://t.co/fB3OyTnFFX
We have not been given the opportunity to discuss nor debate this issue. My constituents deserve to be heard and, if there are any concerns, they should originate at a state level, according to what the people of Puerto Rico- which I proudly represent- decide.
Additionally, an abrupt prohibition of cockfighting will transform a highly regulated industry into an underground industry, bringing back the fights to our streets where there is no control.
The proposed prohibition of cockfighting in the territories would distress even more the economy in Puerto Rico by not only reducing economic activity and jobs, but also the revenues the government collects from licensing and penalties.
These numbers may seem insignificant within the context of the Mainland, but in a depressed economy like Puerto Rico’s, $18 million is a significant amount.
According to the latest statistics from the Puerto Rico Cockfighting Affairs Office, this industry represents:	• Approximately 27 thousand direct and indirect jobs between 82 venues.	• And over $18 million in economic activity, counting only the gaming side.
Originally regulated in 1933, the industry is covered by local Act 98 of 2007, which created the Cockfighting Affairs Office under the Puerto Rico Department of Sports and Recreation, which issued Regulation No. 7424.
This amendment is based on the premise of establishing more Federal regulation over activities in the territories.   In Puerto Rico, cockfighting is already a highly regulated gaming industry.
Today, I rise in respectful opposition to amendment number 28 to H.R. 2, the Agriculture and Nutrition Act of 2018, introduced by the gentleman from the 6th Congressional District of Illinois, Mr. Peter Roskam.
I’ll be on the @HouseFloor discussing my opposition to the amendment banning cockfighting in the U.S. territories. Follow along here: https://t.co/llqHS5neZi

This will allow my office and the Department of the Family in PR, which administers NAP benefits, to make an educated decision on how to move forward in terms of acquiring benefits and addressing factors that reflect increases in the costs of food items found and purchased on PR https://t.co/z0YYoKlmd6
My amendment requests the Secretary of Agriculture to produce a report on the feasibility and impact of Puerto Rico having its own Thrifty Food Plan. https://t.co/ASr4EDCAeI
Puerto Rico is currently included in the Thrifty Food Plan of the 48 contiguous states. However, Puerto Rico imports most food items sold in stores, which increases the cost families pay when purchasing foods included in their diet.

- Si es turista familiarizase con los protocolos locales de evacuación durante un tsunami.
- Tenga un kit de emergencia para asegurar que usted y su familia estén preparados para sobrevivir solos por al menos 72 horas.
- Crear un plan de comunicación entre su familia para saber como contactarse y encontrarse en el caso de que se separen.
- Crear y practicar un plan de evacuación con su familia. Si usted vive en una zona de tsunami vera los avisos en su comunidad. La familiaridad puede salvar su vida.
@fema De presentarse amenaza de Tsunami, FEMA ofrece los siguientes consejos:
AVISO: @FEMA busca que la ciudadanía esté preparada ante la amenaza de cualquier desastre natural. https://t.co/l2whvRa2h9
•If you are a tourist, familiarize yourself with local tsunami evacuation protocols...		•It is vital to familiarize yourself with tsunami notification information: Tsunami Watch, Tsunami Warning, Tsunami Warning.		Visit https://t.co/WrdBoUkj9y for more information.
•Create a family communications plan to know how you’ll contact each other &amp; reconnect if separated. Establish a family meeting place that’s familiar &amp; easy to find.   	•Build an emergency kit to ensure you and your family are prepared to be on your own for at least 72 hours.
•Create and practice an evacuation plan with your family. If you live in a tsunami evacuation zone you will find signs in your community. Familiarity may save your life. Be able to follow your escape route at night and during inclement weather.
FEMA encourages citizens to protect themselves and their families by taking the following steps to ensure they are ready in the event of a tsunami:
If a major earthquake or landslide occurs close to shore, areas are at greater risk if they are less than 25 feet above sea level and within a mile of the shoreline. The first wave in a series could reach the beach in a few minutes, even before a warning is issued.
According to the National Oceanic &amp; Atmospheric Administration, tsunamis are one of the most powerful &amp; destructive natural forces, delivering a series of extremely long waves which can cause dangerous coastal flooding &amp; powerful currents that can last for several hours or days.
Following an intense earthquake that occurred in the Gulf of Alaska, which prompted tsunami watches, advisories and warnings across many state coastlines, FEMA continues to highlight safety tips for those who live in or visit coastal communities.

The filing deadline to return applications for physical property damage for Hurricanes Irma and María is March 20, 2018.  The deadline to return economic injury applications is June 11, 2018 for Hurricane Irma and June 20, 2018 for Hurricane María.
Loan applications can be downloaded from https://t.co/jIoVKb3HdN.  Completed applications should be returned to a recovery center or mailed to: U.S. Small Business Administration, Processing and Disbursement Center, 14925 Kingsport Road, Fort Worth, TX 76155.
• Personal Financial Statement (SBA Form 413) completed, signed, and dated by the applicant (if a sole proprietorship) and for each principal	• Schedule of Liabilities listing all fixed debts (SBA Form 2202 may be used).
• Complete copies, including all schedules, of the most recent Federal income tax returns for the applicant business; an explanation if not available.	• Hacienda Form 2907, Hacienda Authorization and copy of identification.
• SBA business loan application (Form 5) completed and signed.	• Tax Information Authorization (IRS Form 4506-T), completed and signed by each applicant, principal or affiliated business.
SBA reminds businesses that the following items are required to be submitted with their business disaster loan application:

“Businesses and nonprofit organizations may borrow up to $2 million to repair or replace damaged or destroyed real estate, machinery and equipment, inventory and other business assets,” said SBA Puerto Rico &amp; U.S. Virgin Islands District Director, Yvette T. Collazo.

The Disaster Unemployment Assistance deadline is this Thursday, January 11. To see if you are eligible, please contact the Puerto Rico Department of Labor.
However, not all survivors currently located in TSA hotels will be extended until this deadline. Survivors should contact FEMA or their hotel to see if they have been extended.
The Transitional Sheltering Assistance (TSA) program deadline has been extended until March 20, 2018 for residents of Puerto Rico affected by the hurricanes.
No matter who needs help, if you or a loved one feel overwhelmed or are considering self-harm, please call crisis counseling at Linea PAS 800-981-0023. It is open 24 hours a day, seven days a week.
Tomorrow is the las day to apply for the U.S. Army Corps of Engineers Operation Blue Roof Program. For more information, please contact 1-888-ROOF-BLU.
